#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Mapper code
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/usr/bin/python

import sys

def main():
#Takes line from standard input and prints out lower case
        for line in sys.stdin:
                line = line.strip()
                print line.lower()


#main() func is a recurring feature in all my code
#I like functions better than running the code like a script
#More readable for a human
if __name__ == '__main__':
        main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Shell commands exec via bash script
#Reducer not used here. mapred.reduce.tasks=0 indicates that
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

#variables
TASK_ID=1
TASK_DIR=/user/$USER/s1567343_task_$TASK_ID.out
HDP_DIR=/user/$USER/data
INP_FILES=$HDP_DIR/input/webLarge.txt
RE_INP_DIR=$HDP_DIR/input/lowercase
OUT_DIR=$HDP_DIR/output
LOCAL_DIR=./

rm -R $LOCAL_DIR/output
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR

hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -input $INP_FILES \
 -output $OUT_DIR \
 -mapper mapToLower.py \
 -file mapToLower.py \
 -jobconf mapred.reduce.tasks=0 

#Copy the output to local dir
hdfs dfs -copyToLocal $OUT_DIR $LOCAL_DIR
hdfs dfs -rm $RE_INP_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/part* $RE_INP_DIR
#copy the output to task dir
hdfs dfs -rm $TASK_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/* $TASK_DIR

echo "Done. check local output directory"

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Mapper - just using the unix command 'cat'
#Input is the lower case output from the previous job
#'cat' will emit the results which will be sorted according
#to the key which is the entire line, and this will be sent
#to the reducer. 
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Reducer - recieves sorted output from mapper
#checks if line!=prev_line and prints, else skips
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/usr/bin/python
import sys

def main():
	prev_line = ""

	for line in sys.stdin:
        	line = line.strip()
	        if line != prev_line:
        	        print line
                	prev_line = line

if __name__=='__main__':
	main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Bash script to run this job
#input files = from task 1 output
#output files = saved for next job, task 3 (duplicated_data)
#using 36 reducers(sufficiently large enough to scale) 
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

#variables
TASK_ID=2
TASK_DIR=/user/$USER/s1567343_task_$TASK_ID.out
HDP_DIR=/user/$USER/data
INP_FILES=$HDP_DIR/input/lowercase
OUT_DIR=$HDP_DIR/output
RE_INP_DIR=$HDP_DIR/input/duplicated_data
LOCAL_DIR=./

rm -R output/
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR

hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -input $INP_FILES \
 -output $OUT_DIR \
 -mapper cat \
 -reducer reduceToLower.py \
 -file reduceToLower.py \
 -jobconf mapred.reduce.tasks=36 \
 -jobconf mapred.job.name="Adarsh's Job" \

hdfs dfs -copyToLocal $OUT_DIR $LOCAL_DIR
hdfs dfs -rm $RE_INP_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/part* $RE_INP_DIR
#copy the output to task dir
hdfs dfs -rm $TASK_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/* $TASK_DIR

echo "Done. check local output directory"
#-----------------------------------------------------------

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Mapper - wc (unix command for word count)
#We can run wc command on individual mappers and send this
#to a single reducer to sum up
#-----------------------------------------------------------

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Reducer - using unix awk
#it will sum up the line count and word count from each
#mapper output and print out the results
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

awk '{sumW+=$2} {sumL+=$1} END {print sumW, sumL}'

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Bash script to run the commands
#input dir = duplicated data produced from prev job
#number of reducer tasks = 1 . to combine all outputs into a 
#single reducer for summation
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

#variables
TASK_ID=3
TASK_DIR=/user/$USER/s1567343_task_$TASK_ID.out
HDP_DIR=/user/$USER/data
OUT_DIR=$HDP_DIR/output
INP_FILES=$HDP_DIR/input/duplicated_data
LOCAL_DIR=./

rm -R output/
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR

#reduce to a single task only
hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -input $INP_FILES \
 -output $OUT_DIR \
 -mapper wc \
 -reducer reducerSumWc.sh \
 -file reducerSumWc.sh \
 -jobconf mapred.reduce.tasks=1 \
 -jobconf mapred.job.name="Adarsh'sJob" 

hdfs dfs -copyToLocal $OUT_DIR $LOCAL_DIR
#copy the output to task dir
hdfs dfs -rm $TASK_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/* $TASK_DIR

echo "Done. check local output directory"
Task 3 code end

Task 4 code begin

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Mapper - forms word pairs and emits count of 1 for each
#We are adding an aggregatorKey=LongValueSum as we are going
#to use the inbuilt hadoop streaming aggregator class to sum
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/usr/bin/python

import sys

def main():
	#we are going to use the inbuilt aggregate package in hadoop streaming.
	#LongValueSum is the keyword associated with suming up the results associated with that keyword.
	aggregatorKey='LongValueSum:'
        for line in sys.stdin:
                line = line.strip()
		words = line.split()
                for i in range(len(words)-1):
			print aggregatorKey+words[i]+' '+words[i+1]+'\t'+'1'

if __name__ == '__main__':
        main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Bash script to run the commands
#reducer= aggregate - in built func to sum up for single key
#input files = duplicated data
#output = we could use results from this run or Task 5 for 
#the calculation in task 6. so we will save that in 
#word_pairs folder for use in task 6.
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

#variables
TASK_ID=4
TASK_DIR=/user/$USER/s1567343_task_$TASK_ID.out
HDP_DIR=/user/$USER/data
INP_FILES=$HDP_DIR/input/duplicated_data
RE_INP_DIR=$HDP_DIR/input/word_pairs
OUT_DIR=$HDP_DIR/output
LOCAL_DIR=./

rm -R output/
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR

hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -input $INP_FILES \
 -output $OUT_DIR \
 -mapper mapTwoWords.py \
 -file mapTwoWords.py \
 -reducer aggregate \
 -jobconf mapred.reduce.tasks=50 \
 -jobconf mapred.job.name="Adarsh's Job"

hdfs dfs -copyToLocal $OUT_DIR/part-00000 $LOCAL_DIR
hdfs dfs -rm $RE_INP_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/part* $RE_INP_DIR
#copy the output to task dir
hdfs dfs -rm $TASK_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/* $TASK_DIR

echo "Done. check local output directory"

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Mapper - exact same mapper as Task 4
#Reducer and Combiner are using the hadoop stream classes
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/usr/bin/python

import sys

def main():
	#we are going to use the inbuilt aggregate package in hadoop streaming.
	#LongValueSum is the keyword associated with suming up the results associated with that keyword.
	aggregatorKey='LongValueSum:'
        for line in sys.stdin:
                line = line.strip()
		words = line.split()
                for i in range(len(words)-1):
			print aggregatorKey+words[i]+' '+words[i+1]+'\t'+'1'

if __name__ == '__main__':
        main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Bash script to run the commands
#Combiner=aggregate - built in func to sum up for single key
#Reducer=aggregate - same built in func
#Number of reducers = 50. scalable soln
#inp dir= duplicated data
#output dir=word_pairs which will be used for Task 6
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

#variables
TASK_ID=5
TASK_DIR=/user/$USER/s1567343_task_$TASK_ID.out
HDP_DIR=/user/$USER/data
INP_FILES=$HDP_DIR/input/duplicated_data
RE_INP_DIR=$HDP_DIR/input/word_pairs
OUT_DIR=$HDP_DIR/output
LOCAL_DIR=./

rm -R output/
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR

hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -input $INP_FILES \
 -output $OUT_DIR \
 -mapper mapTwoWordsWithCombiner.py \
 -file mapTwoWordsWithCombiner.py \
 -combiner aggregate \
 -reducer aggregate \
 -jobconf mapred.reduce.tasks=50 \
 -jobconf mapred.job.name="Adarsh'sJob"

hdfs dfs -copyToLocal $OUT_DIR $LOCAL_DIR
hdfs dfs -rm $RE_INP_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/part* $RE_INP_DIR

echo "Done. check local output directory"

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Performance - HDP stats
#Job Counters
#Killed map tasks=4
#Launched map tasks=40
#Launched reduce tasks=50
#Data-local map tasks=28
#Rack-local map tasks=12
#Total time spent by all maps in occupied slots (ms)=9848040
#Total time spent by all reduces in occupied slots (ms)=24335616
#Total time spent by all map tasks (ms)=1231005
#Total time spent by all reduce tasks (ms)=3041952
#Performance - Analysis
#Task 4 vs Task 5:
#Total time taken Task 4 = 1608264/43 + 3349724/50=104395 ms
#Total time taken Task 5 = 1330223/40 + 3127638/50=95808 ms 
#Clearly significant performance improvement by using Combiners
#-----------------------------------------------------------

#!/bin/bash

sort -k3rn|head -20

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Mapper and reducer are the same function. Sorts and outputs
#top 20 from among its own input. 
#number of reducers =1. Final list has to be sorted at a 
#single process
#We can have many mappers running to send sorted lists of 20
#to a single reducer to process, so this can be scalable
#Input files - output  from task 5 or task 4
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

#variables
TASK_ID=6
TASK_DIR=/user/$USER/s1567343_task_$TASK_ID.out
HDP_DIR=/user/$USER/data
INP_FILES=$HDP_DIR/input/word_pairs
OUT_DIR=$HDP_DIR/output
LOCAL_DIR=./

rm -R output/
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR

#Running the same map and reduce command but reducing to a single reducer.
hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -input $INP_FILES \
 -output $OUT_DIR \
 -mapper mapReduce.sh \
 -reducer mapReduce.sh \
 -file mapReduce.sh \
 -jobconf mapred.reduce.tasks=1 \
 -jobconf mapred.job.name="Adarsh'sJob"

hdfs dfs -copyToLocal $OUT_DIR $LOCAL_DIR
#copy the output to task dir
hdfs dfs -rm $TASK_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/* $TASK_DIR

echo "Done. check local output directory"

Task 7 code begin

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Mapper - prints out Column index, row index and value
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/usr/bin/python

import sys

def main():
	for line in sys.stdin:
		line = line.strip()
		col_index = 0
		#first value in the line is the row_index
		row_index, line =line.split('\t') 
		for c in line.split():
			print str(col_index) + '\t' + row_index + '\t' + c
			col_index +=1

if __name__ == '__main__':
	main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Reducer - Values arrive sorted according to column and rows
#We will emit each value in the matrix as and when we recv it
#when we hit a new column, we will print a new line and continue
#column index will be printed first to indicate which column
#in the original matrix this row is coming from.
#if we run this on multiple reducers, we can use the column number
#to re order the output from the reducer
#because values arrive sorted by row as well, they will be
#printed in order
#-----------------------------------------------------------

#!/usr/bin/python

import sys
def main():
        prev_col = ''
        firstLine = True #flag to check if this is the first row for this reducer
        for line in sys.stdin:
                line = line.strip()
                col_index, row_index, matrix_val = line.split('\t')
                if col_index == prev_col:
                        #using stdout.write to ensure we dont hit buffer overflow 
                        #we emit the values as soon as we hit them
                        #stdout.write will continue append on the existing output
                        sys.stdout.write(matrix_val + ' ')
                        prev_col = col_index
                else:
                        if not(firstLine):#only print the new line if this is not the first line
                                sys.stdout.write('\n')#new column, new line
                        sys.stdout.write(col_index +'\t'+ matrix_val + ' ')
                        prev_col = col_index
                        firstLine = False
        sys.stdout.write('\n')#new line after the last val has been printed

if __name__ == '__main__':
        main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Bash script to run the commmand
#Mapper and reducer as described above
#This job will involve 2 Mapreduce jobs
#Job1 - do the matrix inverse on mulitple reducers
#number of key fields = 2 -->col_index and row_index
#The mapper output will be sorted on -k1n -k2n 
#this means: num sort col_index, followed by num sort row_index
#Number of reducers = 5. Partitioner splits the vals
#along column number. to re generate a single file from multiple 
#reducer outputs, simple concat will not work. We will use a 2nd
#MapReduce job for that
#Job2 - concat the matrix output into a single file (sorted)
#We will simply use unix command 'cat' to output the contents
#from mappers and reducer. Since mapper output is sorted by hadoop
#we know that the single reducer will receive sorted rows
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

#variables
TASK_ID=7
TASK_DIR=/user/$USER/s1567343_task_$TASK_ID.out
HDP_DIR=/user/$USER/data
INP_FILES=$HDP_DIR/input/matrixLarge.txt
OUT_DIR=$HDP_DIR/output
OUT_DIR_2=$HDP_DIR/output_2
LOCAL_DIR=./

rm -R ./output
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR_2

hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -D mapred.reduce.tasks=1 \
 -D mapreduce.job.output.key.comparator.class=org.apache.hadoop.mapreduce.lib.partition.KeyFieldBasedComparator \
 -D stream.num.map.output.key.fields=2 \
 -D num.key.fields.for.partition=1 \
 -D mapreduce.partition.keypartitioner.options=-k1,1 \
 -D mapreduce.partition.keycomparator.options='-k1n -k2n' \
 -input $INP_FILES \
 -output $OUT_DIR \
 -mapper mapMatrixInv.py \
 -file mapMatrixInv.py \
 -reducer reduceMatrixInv.py \
 -file reduceMatrixInv.py \
 -partitioner org.apache.hadoop.mapred.lib.KeyFieldBasedPartitioner

hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -D mapred.reduce.tasks=1 \
 -D mapreduce.job.output.key.comparator.class=org.apache.hadoop.mapreduce.lib.partition.KeyFieldBasedComparator \
 -D stream.num.map.output.key.fields=1 \
 -D num.key.fields.for.partition=1 \
 -D mapreduce.partition.keypartitioner.options=-k1,1 \
 -D mapreduce.partition.keycomparator.options='-k1n' \
 -input $OUT_DIR \
 -output $OUT_DIR_2 \
 -mapper cat \
 -reducer cat

hdfs dfs -copyToLocal $OUT_DIR_2 $LOCAL_DIR
#copy the output to task dir
hdfs dfs -rm $TASK_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR_2/* $TASK_DIR

echo "Done. check local output directory"

Task 8 code begin

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Mapper - if student emit the first 3 chars
# if marks (not student), emit 4 chars
# key will be the student Id in each case
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/usr/bin/python

import sys

def main():
	for line in sys.stdin:
		line = line.strip()
		line = line.split()
		#making the student id col the key variable
		if line[0] == 'student':
			emit([line[1],line[0],line[2]])
		else:
			emit([line[2],line[0],line[1],line[3]])
		
def emit(items):
	stringOutput = ''
	for item in items:
		stringOutput += item + '\t'
	print stringOutput.strip()


if __name__ == '__main__':
	main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Reducer - takes sorted input from mapper, and waits for 
#student name and marks
#as input is sorted according to student id, will emit once
#we hit the new student id
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/usr/bin/python

import sys

def main():
	prev_student_id = ''
	course_list = []
	for line in sys.stdin:
		line = line.strip()
		line = line.split('\t')
		student_id= line[0] #the key
		if student_id == prev_student_id:
			if line[1] == 'student':
				student_name = line[2]
			else:
				course_list.append((line[2],line[3]))
		else:
			if prev_student_id:
				printStudentDetails(student_name,course_list)
			prev_student_id = student_id
			course_list = []
			if line[1] == 'student':
				student_name = line[2]
			else:
				course_list.append((line[2],line[3]))
	
	#for the last row
	printStudentDetails(student_name, course_list)

def printStudentDetails(student_name, course_list):
	stringOutput = student_name + ' -->'
	for (course_name, course_marks) in course_list:
		stringOutput += ' ('+course_name+','+course_marks+')'
	print stringOutput

if __name__ == '__main__':
	main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Bash script to run the commands
#Mappers and reducers as defined above
#number of reduce task = 50. sufficiently large to scale
#Results from this will be saved to studentdata folder
#to be used for Task 9
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

#variables
TASK_ID=8
TASK_DIR=/user/$USER/s1567343_task_$TASK_ID.out
HDP_DIR=/user/$USER/data
INP_FILES=$HDP_DIR/input/uniLarge.txt
RE_INP_DIR=$HDP_DIR/input/studentdata
OUT_DIR=$HDP_DIR/output
LOCAL_DIR=./

rm -R ./output
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR

hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -input $INP_FILES \
 -output $OUT_DIR \
 -mapper mapStudentMarks.py \
 -file mapStudentMarks.py \
 -reducer reduceStudentMarks.py \
 -file reduceStudentMarks.py \
 -jobconf mapred.reduce.tasks=50 \

hdfs dfs -rm $RE_INP_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/part* $RE_INP_DIR
hdfs dfs -copyToLocal $OUT_DIR $LOCAL_DIR
#copy the output to task dir
hdfs dfs -rm $TASK_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/* $TASK_DIR

echo "Done. check local output directory"

Task 9 code begin

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Mapper - Take the input from task 8 output 
#Find those lines which are greater than 2+4=6 items long
#because first 2 items in line are student name and '-->'
#We only need to emit lines which have more than 4 courses
#Then we identify the student with the lowest avg in this 
#mapper. and emit that out at the end
#Should be able to handle multiple minima 
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/usr/bin/python

import sys

def main():
	lowest_avg = 0
	lowest_avg_student_list = []
	for line in sys.stdin:
		line = line.strip()
		line = line.split()
		totalMarks = 0
		numCourses = 0
		if len(line) > (2+4):
		#first two items are name and --> symbol. after that the marks
			for item in line:
				if '(' in item: #hacky way of finding the marks
					item = removeBrackets(item)
					course_name, course_mark = item.split(',')
					totalMarks += float(course_mark.strip())
					numCourses += 1
			avg = totalMarks/numCourses
			if (not(lowest_avg)) or (avg < lowest_avg):#if lowest avg is not initialized or avg is lesser than lowest avg
				lowest_avg = avg
                                lowest_avg_student_list = [line[0]] #reinitialize to the lowest val
                        elif avg == lowest_avg: # we need to append student name to the list
                                lowest_avg_student_list.append(line[0])
        #this should work for more than one student with the lowest avg
        for lowest_avg_student in lowest_avg_student_list:
                emit([lowest_avg_student, lowest_avg])
		
def emit(items):
	stringOutput = ''
	for item in items:
		stringOutput += str(item) + '\t'
	print stringOutput.strip()

def removeBrackets(item):
	return item.replace('(','').replace(')','')

if __name__ == '__main__':
	main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Reduce - reduced input from mappers
#We take those inputs and find the min again
#This should be able to handle multi minima points
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/usr/bin/python

import sys

def main():
	lowest_avg = 0
	for line in sys.stdin:
		line = line.strip()
		line = line.split('\t')
		student_name= line[0] #the key
		student_avg= line[1] #the value
		if not(lowest_avg) or (student_avg <lowest_avg):
			lowest_avg = student_avg
			lowest_avg_student_list = [student_name] #re initialize to lowest val
                elif student_avg == lowest_avg: #handles 2 or more students with low avg
                        lowest_avg_student_list.append(student_name)

        #ASSUMPTION: we run this only on a single reducer
        for lowest_avg_student in lowest_avg_student_list:
                print lowest_avg_student + ' with ' + lowest_avg

if __name__ == '__main__':
	main()

#-----------------------------------------------------------
#Bash script to run the commands
#Input dir - student data from task 8
#Number of reducers =1 so final min can happen at one proc
#-----------------------------------------------------------
#!/bin/bash

#variables
TASK_ID=1
TASK_DIR=/user/$USER/s1567343_task_$TASK_ID.out
HDP_DIR=/user/$USER/data
INP_FILES=$HDP_DIR/input/studentdata
OUT_DIR=$HDP_DIR/output
LOCAL_DIR=./

rm -R ./output
hdfs dfs -rm -R $OUT_DIR

hadoop jar /opt/hadoop/hadoop-2.7.1/share/hadoop/tools/lib/hadoop-streaming-2.7.1.jar \
 -input $INP_FILES \
 -output $OUT_DIR \
 -mapper mapLowestAvg.py \
 -file mapLowestAvg.py \
 -reducer reduceLowestAvg.py \
 -file reduceLowestAvg.py \
 -jobconf mapred.reduce.tasks=1

hdfs dfs -copyToLocal $OUT_DIR $LOCAL_DIR
#copy the output to task dir
hdfs dfs -rm $TASK_DIR/*
hdfs dfs -cp $OUT_DIR/* $TASK_DIR

echo "Done. check local output directory"
